<div id="review_256833206" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/256833206" />
    <a title="Ava Brightly ☕" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4975085-ava-brightly"><img alt="Ava Brightly ☕" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593276482p2/4975085.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/256833206?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ava Brightly ☕" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ava Brightly ☕" href="/user/show/4975085-ava-brightly">Ava Brightly ☕</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4975085-ava-brightly?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4975085-ava-brightly?shelf=science-fiction-fantasy">science-fiction-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4975085-ava-brightly?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4975085-ava-brightly?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer256833206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6357856333072450576">Update 8 July 2014:<br/><br/>**NO SPOILERS but may contain spoilers of earlier books in the series**<br/><br/>It's taken me some time to absorb this story. You know how a story just sticks to you for days, like peanut butter on the roof of your mouth or more dryer socks to your mind and you peel back the layers of characters and detail and you get sparks and snaps and you rabbit trail in your brain and off you go in thought and end up writing a review with the longest run-on sentence on the planet this side of the </span>
  <span id="freeText6357856333072450576" style="display:none">Update 8 July 2014:<br /><br />**NO SPOILERS but may contain spoilers of earlier books in the series**<br /><br />It's taken me some time to absorb this story. You know how a story just sticks to you for days, like peanut butter on the roof of your mouth or more dryer socks to your mind and you peel back the layers of characters and detail and you get sparks and snaps and you rabbit trail in your brain and off you go in thought and end up writing a review with the longest run-on sentence on the planet this side of the Bulwer-Lytton Fiction Contest?<br /><br />That's me after reading Diana Gabaldon's latest installment in the Outlander series.<br /><br />The writing is fantastic. This is why I love her books. It's not singularly romance, science fiction, adventure, history, time travel, or cultures and war. And yet, it's ALL of those things. <br /><br />I had the pleasure of seeing her at a signing last week (autographed book!!) and during her lecture, she mentioned people ask her if there is anyone else she could recommend that writes as she does. She doesn't and I agree wholeheartedly. <br /><br />Her writing is brilliant: carefully crafted detail in each setting and the minutiae of senses, sight, sound, taste, touch, and smell, the intricacies of relationships and characters so well developed, to love or despise, to weep with or need to conquer. These characters feel like live, warm bodies standing before me as tangible as one of my family.<br /><br />This is why the pages kept turning without any daunting hesitation, all 825 of them. <br /><br />I felt out of the entire series, this is the best to date. Picking up where An Echo In The Bone left off, the story took off. More peril, adventure, warm tender moments, loyalties tried, and eye-popping moments.<br /><br />I don't want to spoil anything so here are a few points that stuck in my brain.<br /><br />Jamie and Claire are imperfectly perfect. Sigh. Their conversations, even discussing the mundane, are words spoken with an undercurrent of myriad emotion and a familiarity without a comfortable monotony. They love each other to self-sacrifice but also blanketed with respect to allow each other to be who they are as a person with convictions, even those seared to the bone and the core of their being. <br /><br />True historical characters making their appearance was incredibly fun. If I was Claire, I'd be floored to be standing in the same room as a couple of key figures in the American Revolutionary War. As a genealogist, I've researched my own 6th time great grandfather back to a clerk to Gen. George Washington, so it was amazing to think of my own ancestor in this time period experiencing what I was reading.<br /><br />William. He's growing up. The relationship between him and his father, and also with Lord John, hanging in the balance and leaving me asking when the next book was going to be released. William had such a time in this book. Frying pan, fire, deep in the coals. Oh, William...so much like his fathers, what path do you have before you? <br /><br />I know, I know. I'm being a greedy. Diana probably hasn't taken a good solid breath since this release. :) <br /><br />Bree and Roger. I can't give away spoilers but I will say that Roger also comes across a character we haven't met. Roger has an encounter that made me almost yell, "HOLY SCHEISSE!" (I curse in German. Don't ask) <br /><br />As for Bree, we saw a lot of her father's character and her mother's determination. "Bree" rather aptly means "storm". Mess with her family, and she'll start kicking ass and taking names. <br /><br />Young Ian was particularly interesting to me because the reader got to see a side of him that is so decidedly Mohawk. He is grown from the very young man we saw in Voyager. In past installments, we saw and heard stories from his life as a Mohawk, but to see the Mohawk and Scot culmination of principals, upbringing, and character so pointedly displayed in a certain moment literally made me gasp. I had to read it three times to absorb how incredible that moment unfolded. Ian's all grown up now. Mohawk and Scot. Powerful writing. <br /><br />There are so many great moments with Lord John and many of the returning cast of characters, I couldn't possibly touch on all of them. <br /><br />Overall, this is definitely one of the best in the series, probably my favorite next to the first, Outlander. I highly, highly recommend this series. <br /><br />(PS. My hubs likened these to one of his favorite series, Bernard Cornwell's Sharpe's books. I'd love to hear if that is a common consensus.)<br /><br /><br />***<br />Update 2 Jun 2014:<br />8 days (or 7 sleeps, 6hrs, 25 min, and 25 seconds... or 23 meals... or 627,925 seconds... or 10,465 minutes... or 174 hours. ) and counting down. Do you know where your pre-order is?<br /><br />***<br />NOoooooooo! March 2014! A curse to three more extended months. <br /><br />A pox to three more months! I banish three months from all publisher's catalogs! I abhor, disrespect, denounce, and give a giant flush to the literary toilet of all extended months. <br /><br />May those extended months get sunburned and attract ants in their picnic. I proclaim an epic Hamlet-ing and George RR Martin-ing the characters of three more months. May those extended months have stupid boring weekends, become plagued with 47 cats, and come down with epic random patterned baldness! And if those months attempt escape, may they be flogged to an inch of their life, hung from their scrawny necks, trampled by cattle, and buried in a shallow grave.<br /><br />May their Plenty Of Fish profile only be hit on by the ugly and unemployed. And the tags removed from their short-sheeted mattresses. May their kilts be drafty, corsets too tight, and their beer sour and stale! As their hard tack becomes maggot infested, I wish these months nothing but stomach churning sea sickness. I curse upon their days the smell of old eggs and buttermilk, that it permeate saddle blankets of all extended months while the fleas from 1,000 camels lodge in their crotchal regions. <br /><br />(and something else about elderberries, hamsters and farting in their general direction).<br /><br />I understand patience and polishing the craft that flows from the deliciously wicked pen of Diana Gabaldon, I still do not have to like it.<br /><br />New Release Date - aka New Date That Shall Not Be Named: 25 March 2014. <br /><br />Thats NDTSNBN to you.<br /><br />Regardless, Diana Gabaldon's books are always worth the wait, even until NDTSNBN. Well researched, beautifully written, and typically a hefty addition to this amazing series. This still does not mean I have to like NDTSNBN. So I will pick my undignified self off the floor, wipe my tears, and gird my loins for NDTSNBN. <br /><br />Since I have to wait. And I will. Patiently.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6357856333072450576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/249893914?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karla" href="/user/show/3024056-karla">Karla</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer249893914" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11557765680451136531"><br/><b>5 Glorious Stars, then 5 more and then another 5!! Without question, the best book in this amazing series and I don’t even know how that’s possible, since the entire series as a whole is SUPERB! Would I want to wait 4 years+ for the next installment?? ABSOLUTELY NOT...but this was worth every second that ticked on the clock until it was released!! Diana Gabaldon poured her <i>heart</i> along with some of her <i>own blood</i> into this book!!</b> <br/><br/><b>
  <i>**Spoiler free review**</i>
</b><br/><br/>There is heartache in this book, but it w</span>
  <span id="freeText11557765680451136531" style="display:none"><br /><b>5 Glorious Stars, then 5 more and then another 5!! Without question, the best book in this amazing series and I don’t even know how that’s possible, since the entire series as a whole is SUPERB! Would I want to wait 4 years+ for the next installment?? ABSOLUTELY NOT...but this was worth every second that ticked on the clock until it was released!! Diana Gabaldon poured her <i>heart</i> along with some of her <i>own blood</i> into this book!!</b> <br /><br /><b>
  <i>**Spoiler free review**</i>
</b><br /><br />There is heartache in this book, but it will also bring about tremendous joy and happiness for readers who love this series. The ending alone sucked the air right out of my lungs and made me sob like a baby, but they were tears of utter delight and satisfaction! <br /><br />There are so many moments in this book...heartwarming, achingly beautiful moments, that will choke you up. Moments that are peaceful and comforting...family milling about, doing everyday family things, nothing exciting, but so important for the reader to connect to the characters. Moments of great sadness...that will bring you to your knees, where you will mourn alongside the characters you've come to love. Defining moments... that are never outwardly stated, but through Diana Gabaldon's beautiful words, secrets are revealed and the story and the lives of these characters continues to unfold. The execution is flawless and she doesn't miss a beat! <br /><br /><i>Written in My Own Heart's Blood</i> is intensely detailed, and at times very graphic. The author doesn't hold back when it comes to the ravages of war, just as she doesn't deny us in describing the passion that many so many of the couples feel in this book. While some scenes made me cringe and hurt for those who suffered, others were so incredibly sweet and lovely, they warm you from the inside out. <br /><br />She also has a wonderful sense of humor, and it surfaces at times when the reader needs the comic relief, and while it might not always seem like time to laugh or smile, DG knows when to give readers a break from their emotions. <br /><br />This book, as well as the others in the series, is all consuming. <b>You don't just read this book, you experience it, you feel it, you live it, and absorb it into your soul! </b> Outlander will forever be my favorite series and this well could become my favorite book. My only hope is that our wait for the next installment is not quite as long as it was for <i>Written in My Own Hearts Blood</i>. I understand the need to take the time to write a book as detailed as this one, but please Diana Gabaldon, I beg of you don't torture us like this again! My clock is ticking as well as yours, I think you know what I mean! <br /><br /><b>The audiobook version...5 Huge Stars!</b><br />I had the utmost pleasure of listening to Davina Porter and her brilliant narration. When I first started to listen to this series on audio I thought her voice was too mature for these characters, most especially Claire. Boy was I wrong. She might well have the largest body of characters in any series to find voices for, a difficult task and she does it with the utmost perfection. She manages to give recognizable voices to all the familiar characters and introduce new ones, and each and every one is different and distinguishable. She injects an amazing amount of emotion into the dialogue, but also into the descriptive detail. It's as if she was born to read this series and Diana Gabaldon wrote it for her to read! <br /><br /><b>**A side note**</b> As an American, and a long time resident of NJ, the Revolutionary War aspect of this book was intriguing and fascinating. While it might not hold as much interest for some readers, it was one of the highlights in the book for me. I've walked on the ground where so many of the men and women depicted in this book have walked before me and where their blood was shed. I felt sadness in my heart for all who were lost and suffered unimaginable injuries, but also have a great appreciation and respect for those who fought for our freedom. <br /><br /><i>Let the countdown to the TV show begin!! </i><br /><br />***I found an ooops! Did anyone else see that too! Don't read this if you haven't read the book! <b>Major spoiler.</b><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[John's comment to Dottie about Ian surviving his wound, when he was clearly at the wedding ceremony. No biggie, just think DG should call her editors out on that one. I know she doesn't write the book in order that we read it. She writes scenes and then pieces the story together, but it was pretty obvious and my GR friend Jill verified it for me. I wanted to make sure I wasn't just confused...so much going on! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>***</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5544835583167676289">Written in My Own Heart's Blood (Outlander #8), Diana Gabaldon<br/><br/>The British evacuation of Philadelphia and the ensuing Battle of Monmouth are the major events from the book based on real history. It is June 1778, Philadelphia and Jamie Fraser has just returned from the dead, and the world seems to be turning upside-down. The British Army is withdrawing from Philadelphia, with George Washington in pursuit, and for the first time, it looks as if the rebels might actually win. But for Claire Fraser a</span>
  <span id="freeText5544835583167676289" style="display:none">Written in My Own Heart's Blood (Outlander #8), Diana Gabaldon<br /><br />The British evacuation of Philadelphia and the ensuing Battle of Monmouth are the major events from the book based on real history. It is June 1778, Philadelphia and Jamie Fraser has just returned from the dead, and the world seems to be turning upside-down. The British Army is withdrawing from Philadelphia, with George Washington in pursuit, and for the first time, it looks as if the rebels might actually win. But for Claire Fraser and her family, there are even more tumultuous revolutions that have to be accommodated. Her former husband, Jamie, has returned from the dead, demanding to know why in his absence she married his best friend, Lord John Grey. Lord John's son, the ninth Earl of Ellesmere, is no less shocked to discover that his real father is actually the newly resurrected Jamie Fraser, and Jamie's nephew Ian Murray discovers that his new-found cousin has an eye for the woman who has just agreed to marry him. And while Claire is terrified that one of her husbands may be about to murder the other, in the 20th century her descendants face even more desperate turns of events. Her daughter Brianna is trying to protect her son from a vicious criminal with murder on his mind, while her husband Roger has disappeared into the past. <br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز پانزدهم ماه آوریل سال 2018 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: بیگانه (غریبه): کتاب هشتم: نوشته شده با خون قلبم؛ نویسنده: دایانا گبلدون؛<br /><br />عقب نشینی آرتش انگلستان از «فیلادلفیا»، و نبرد پس از آن در «مونموت»، رویدادهای این کتاب هستند؛ که بر اساس رویدادهای راستین تاریخی نگاشته شده اند؛ اکنون ماه ژوئن سال 1778 میلادی، در دیار «فیلادلفیا» است، «جیمی فریزر» به تازگی از دیار مردگان بازگشته است، و به نظر میرسد، که جهان وارونه شده است؛ آرتش انگلیس، از «فیلادلفیا» عقب نشینی کرده، و «جورج واشنگتن» در پیگرد آنهاست؛ و برای نخستین بار چنین به دیده مینشیند، که شورشیان هم میتوانند برنده باشند. اما برای «کلر فریزر»، و خانواده اش، دلنگرانی و خیالهای پرشورتری نیز وجود دارند، همسر وی «جیمی»، از دیار مردگان برگشته، و خواستار دانستن اینست، که چرا او در غیاب وی، با بهترین دوستش، «لرد جان گری» ازدواج کرد؛ پسر «لرد جان»، نهمین «ارل الزمیر»، از کشف این راستی که پدر وی «جیمی فریزر» تازه زنده شده، و «یان موری»، خواهرزاده ی «جیمی»، درمییابد که پسر عموی تازه یافته اش، چشم به زنی دارد، که ازدواج با او را پذیرفته است؛ در حالیکه «کلر» میترسد، که یکی از همسرانش، خیال کشتار آن دیگری را داشته باشند، در سده ی بیستم میلادی، فرزندان وی با رخدادهای ناامیدانه ی بسیاری، روبرو شده اند؛ دختر او «برایانا»، در حال تلاش برای نگهداری از پسرش، در برابر یک جنایتکار شرور است، در حالیکه همسرش «راجر» در گذشته ناپدید شده است؛ و...؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_899082545" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/899082545" />
    <a title="B the BookAddict" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19832827-b-the-bookaddict"><img alt="B the BookAddict" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478463572p2/19832827.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/899082545?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B the BookAddict" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B the BookAddict" href="/user/show/19832827-b-the-bookaddict">B the BookAddict</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer4927987844698566675"><br/>In this eighth instalment and penultimate book of the Outlander series, we are treated to the great rollicking, rip-snorting ride we've come to expect from Diana Gabaldon. It's a <i>step aboard and hang on to your hat</i> experience that lifts you from the humdrum of normal life and takes you deep within the <i>Fraser</i> experience. As well as all the normal cast of characters, we have George Washington, Benedict Arnold and Charles Lee as the battle of the US Revoltuionary War heats up. Gabaldon has cleverly</span>
  <span id="freeText4927987844698566675" style="display:none"><br />In this eighth instalment and penultimate book of the Outlander series, we are treated to the great rollicking, rip-snorting ride we've come to expect from Diana Gabaldon. It's a <i>step aboard and hang on to your hat</i> experience that lifts you from the humdrum of normal life and takes you deep within the <i>Fraser</i> experience. As well as all the normal cast of characters, we have George Washington, Benedict Arnold and Charles Lee as the battle of the US Revoltuionary War heats up. Gabaldon has cleverly written this as a stand alone novel, so no prior experience of the Outlander series is necessary. Unlike many, my own favorite characters are Brianna, Ian and Roger. The tragic death of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Henri-Christian <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> left a huge lump in my throat; what a delightful character he was, I loved him. My quibble is that having already suspended our belief by the magic of the stones, why didn't Gabaldon let <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rollo <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> live? Reading this novel, I alternately laughed, cried, held my breath and cheered the characters on. Altogether a <i>gobsmack-ingly</i> good read and one I would highly recommend. 5★<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4927987844698566675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_947786914" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/947786914" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10436494-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384798006p2/10436494.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/947786914?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/10436494-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer947786914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11148417630254591230">EPIC!!<br/><br/><i>"I have loved others, and I do love many, Sassenach-but you alone hold all my heart, whole in your hands," he said softly. "And you know that."</i><br/><br/><br/> <b>I have loved ye since I saw you, Sassenach,"</b><br/> <b>he said very quietly, holding my eyes with his own, bloodshot and lined with tiredness but very blue. "I will love ye forever. It doesa matter if ye sleep with the whole English army- well, no," he corrected himself, "it would matter, but I wouldna stop me love you."</b><br/><br/>Diana Gabaldon does not disappoint wit</span>
  <span id="freeText11148417630254591230" style="display:none">EPIC!!<br /><br /><i>"I have loved others, and I do love many, Sassenach-but you alone hold all my heart, whole in your hands," he said softly. "And you know that."</i><br /><br /><br /> <b>I have loved ye since I saw you, Sassenach,"</b><br /> <b>he said very quietly, holding my eyes with his own, bloodshot and lined with tiredness but very blue. "I will love ye forever. It doesa matter if ye sleep with the whole English army- well, no," he corrected himself, "it would matter, but I wouldna stop me love you."</b><br /><br />Diana Gabaldon does not disappoint with this book. (Like anyone really thought she could, I mean she is a genius)<br /><br />Written in My Own Heart's Blood (or MOBY) was an emotional roller coaster to say the least. I mean that in all the best (and heartbreaking) ways possible. <br /><br />We see several POV's in this book. Of course there is our Jamie and Claire, but we get a good deal of Ian (and Rachel) and also Roger and Bree. And of course William<br /><br />The Roger and Bree story line is the craziest for me. Of course if you read ECHO, you know that Jem was kidnapped by Cameron who is a very bad man. Obviously. I loved the relationship with Mandy and Jem. Of course they are brother and sister, but they have a very interesting connection that you learn more about as the story unfolds.<br /><br />Roger ends up going back to look for Jem (not spoiling) but he ends up in a time BEFORE Jamie and Claire time by a few years. <br /><br />The person who Roger meets, I won't spoil, but I just loved him. I wanted Roger to give the proper warnings, but I knew that he could not do so without drastically changing lives.<br /><br />Ian and Rachel are pretty sweet too. Of course we learned of Ian's fascination with the Quaker girl in ECHO, but it was a little uncertain if they would end up together.<br />This book made me love Ian a whole lot more. He really is just this amazing man that we have seen grow up in this series. He want from being this awkward teenager to this amazing fierce man. And his heart. It's just... He's full of love for those around him. Which we know he gets from his Uncle Jamie.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When Ian and Rachel get married and he lays down what he calls a love token from Emily <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /> <b>"Now I lay it down, as witness that I come here a free man, that my life and my heart are once more mine to give. And I hope I may be allowed now to give them forever." </b><br /><br />William. had a hard time with his portions in ECHO. I did. But at the end his reaction to finding out that Jamie was his father was intense. To be totally honest this book made me fall in love with William, he's an amazing man (just like his Da) but seriously I wanted to punch him a few times and tell him that there were worst men in the world he could discovered had fathered him. I mean his father is Jamie Fraser. Talk about DNA lottery!<br /><br />Jamie and Claire. Oh Jamie.. Okay, we really have to discuss that he has ruined me for all book men. I mean Alexander Barrington, I love you but seriously JAMMF is riding very close behind you.<br /><br />Jamie is the sweetest, most loving and perfect man there is. Of course he isn't perfect, no one claimed he was but you see really get to see him with Claire throughout this book. They are not split up at any point in time that I can recall an I LOVED that. God they spent so much time apart in other books. <br /><br />It's rough in the start of this book. Jamie knows that Claire has slept with John Grey (again not a spoiler if you have read ECHO) and he is basically just trying to wrap his brain around this. <br /><br />************Spoilers************<br />He's more pissed at LJG than he is at Claire. He knew the kind of pain she felt, he had felt it before himself. His reaction to LJG though well I felt LJG even though I really like him, the dude deserved it. <br /><br />We see LJG really not pushing the "I heart Jamie' bandwagon this book. Of course we know he cares for him, but he is fighting his own wars (literally aint no one got time for anything else) He was amazing to Claire, which really made me happy. He really respected her. <br /><br />back to Jamie and how amazing he is.. So again, the love between Jamie and Claire I felt was more pronounced in this book. Yes we know they were in love in all the other books, but in the other books a lot of bad ass shit (sorry) was taking place and the universe seemed to be always ripping these two apart. In this book there is slightly less of that. There's drama in other places, but their love shines! <br /><br />Here are a few of my favorite quotes from Jamie<br /><br /> <b>I have loved ye since I saw you, Sassenach,"</b><br /> <b>he said very quietly, holding my eyes with his own, bloodshot and lined with tiredness but very blue. "I will love ye forever. It doesa matter if ye sleep with the whole English army- well, no," he corrected himself, "it would matter, but I wouldna stop me love you."</b><br /><br />Then<br /><br /> <b>"I don't say that I dinna mind this, because I do. And I don't say that I'll no make a fuss about it later, because likely I will. But what I do say is that there is nothing in this world or the next that can take ye from me- or me from you." He raised one brow. "D'ye disagree?"</b><br /><br />Swoon<br /><br /><b>"Ye lost your parents young, mo nighean donn, and wandered about the world, rootless. Ye loved Frank"- his mouth compressed for an instant, but I thought he was unconscious of it-"and of course you love Brianna and Roger Mac and the weans... but, Sassenach- I am the true home of your heart, and I know that." </b><br /><br />I love him. <br /><br />This series just gets better as it goes. I cannot wait to read book 9 in about 5 years (well worth the wait)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11148417630254591230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_264627147" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/264627147" />
    <a title="Hildy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5033175-hildy"><img alt="Hildy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474498190p2/5033175.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/264627147?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hildy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hildy" href="/user/show/5033175-hildy">Hildy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer264627147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11755625503477161348">SPOILERS BELOW! I CANNA WRITE THIS WITHOUT SPOILERS! I have too much to say. <br/><br/>I am so not worthy to write this review. Diana Gabaldon's writing is just so beautifully descriptive, her characters are so compelling, her plotlines so interwoven, that anything I say is going to seem dumb in comparison. I'm just a reader who has loved every single one of the books in the Outlander series, until now. <br/><br/>I liked this and there were parts that I LOVED but I rarely got to those moments where I couldn't put t</span>
  <span id="freeText11755625503477161348" style="display:none">SPOILERS BELOW! I CANNA WRITE THIS WITHOUT SPOILERS! I have too much to say. <br><br>I am so not worthy to write this review. Diana Gabaldon's writing is just so beautifully descriptive, her characters are so compelling, her plotlines so interwoven, that anything I say is going to seem dumb in comparison. I'm just a reader who has loved every single one of the books in the Outlander series, until now. <br><br>I liked this and there were parts that I LOVED but I rarely got to those moments where I couldn't put this book down. In fact, that was my problem. I kept putting it down and had to sometimes force myself to pick it back up. I've heard some of my friends say that this book was such a roller coaster and that's exactly how I felt when I was reading this book. I just don't think we mean the same thing by that. There were times where it was incredibly exciting and moving, where I could feel my heart rate picking up and I was so exhilarated. Unfortunately, I'd move onto other parts of the book and felt like I was sitting in the loading zone, looking around waiting for something exciting to happen. It kills me to say that, especially when almost every one of my friends have loved this. I'm so happy that you did. I just wish I was one of you.<br><br>Brace yourself, I am about to say the most blasphemous thing that a fan of Diana Gabaldon can say:<br><br><b> I think she needs to hurry up and end this. </b> <br><br>I know you are all reading this, wanting to throw fruit at me and say, "Boo, Hildy! Boo!" This is just one person's opinion. I feel like this is getting unnecessarily drawn out. I know that Claire is a doctor and in every single book we are walked through her surgeries and medical emergencies. Eight books later, I'm tired of it. It bores me. Although, I was geekily excited when she mentioned fistula surgeries because I'd read Cutting For Stone and consider myself a sort of unofficial expert on the topic. ;) Diana's over-use of big words sometimes halts the flow of the writing. I had to Google so many terms and then I'd get distracted by Facebook and not go back to the book. <br><br>I was incredibly impatient reading this. After waiting 4 years and having read the first 7 books one after the other, I really couldn't wait to see where this story was going to go. I spoke to one of my friends (the one person on the planet who agrees with me about this book) and said, "I've waited 4 years and I'm 500 pages in and I feel like not a whole lot is happening." Now, part of this is my fault. Three years ago I read some Dailylines. If I ever try to do that again, someone needs to tackle me, and fast! I ruined some pretty fantastic moments by reading or listening to them ahead of time. One MAJOR plot point was revealed while I was listening to DG read an excerpt in Fergus (Did somebody say FERGUS?) 3 years ago. It was pretty darned brilliant at the time but not so much as I read it in the story. It just didn't have any sort of emotional impact on me at all as I read it. I could kick myself. Also, I got my ass spoiled when I went on a social networking site and saw an important moment with the exact page number that it happened. It went something like this: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ "P.691 of MOBY. My heart is breaking!" I was not impressed. I was fairly certain that in 50 pages, someone important was going to die. Don't do that people. It totally ruined that moment for me. Why? Cause I knew it was coming, even if I didn't know the who of it.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>There were definitely some incredible moments in this book. I loved Roger and Brianna and the kids and I found myself wishing for them to come back in the story, especially when we were reading about Dottie, Hal and Ben (Yawn!). I loved William's story and every time Claire was saving someone I daydreamed about poor, broken, sweet William. As always, I loved Jamie, but I found a lot of his scenes and dialogue to be too short or it ended abruptly, making me a little bitter that I couldn't have more of him. By the end of the story, I was definitely back on the DG train and was loving it. Unfortunately, I just couldn't forget how I felt during most of the first half.<br><br>**EDIT: <i> I just can't get the image of Percy being like photo bomber out of my head! OMG! Am I allowed to crack myself up? Didn't he just pop into important scenes and then leave just as fast? I can just picture him jumping into a photo with a big smile on his face and his head tipped to the side and then bolting. He was never around for very long. LOL!!! </i><br><br>Am I still looking forward to read Book 9? Of COURSE! That's just silly to think otherwise. I will say that I don't have the same anticipation that I had for Book 8.<br><br>I realize that probably a third of our followers are Outlander fans and I am risking life and limb letting my feelings spilleth over here but I'm risking it. I am a wee bit scairt. Somebody hold me. <br> <br><a href="http://s1293.photobucket.com/user/Hildy71/media/blogheader-1_zpsce106f4c.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt=" photo blogheader-1_zpsce106f4c.jpg" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397329596i/9263771._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_388748124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/388748124" />
    <a title="Jane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2679341-jane"><img alt="Jane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442635072p2/2679341.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/388748124?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane" href="/user/show/2679341-jane">Jane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/22443077-written-in-my-own-heart-s-blood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2679341-jane?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer388748124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15682942227776853613">Where I got the book: audiobook purchased on Audible. ***SPOILERS***<br/><br/><i>Written in My Own Heart’s Blood</i> is the eighth of what Diana Gabaldon describes as the Big, Enormous Books of the Outlander series (<a href='http://www.dianagabaldon.com/books/chronology-of-the-outlander-series/ ' rel='nofollow noopener'>this page</a> will show you both the chronology of that series and the fact that she views all the spinoffs as part of the series, thus complicating matters to stratospheric levels). As she ended Big, Enormous Book 7 on a cliffhanger, I and apparently a large portion of the world’s population were eagerl</span>
  <span id="freeText15682942227776853613" style="display:none">Where I got the book: audiobook purchased on Audible. ***SPOILERS***<br /><br /><i>Written in My Own Heart’s Blood</i> is the eighth of what Diana Gabaldon describes as the Big, Enormous Books of the Outlander series (<a href="http://www.dianagabaldon.com/books/chronology-of-the-outlander-series/ " rel="nofollow noopener">this page</a> will show you both the chronology of that series and the fact that she views all the spinoffs as part of the series, thus complicating matters to stratospheric levels). As she ended Big, Enormous Book 7 on a cliffhanger, I and apparently a large portion of the world’s population were eagerly awaiting the Further Revelations that we could quite confidently predict would involve Family Secrets, Amazing Escapes, Sex, Time Travel, Warfare and Grisly Descriptions of Messy Surgery. And I knew that reviewing this book would be difficult, but now I’m sitting down to the task the enormity of trying to encapsulate this Bloody Enormous Book, doorstop, chunkster or kitten squisher in a non-novel-length review is weighing on me.<br /><br />The first overwhelming consideration is, how spoilerish should I be? And I’ve decided I can’t possibly be critical (in the sense of reviewing the good AND bad) without being spoilerish, so the spoilers will start pretty soon. You have been warned.<br /><br />And then I began thinking, as I mentally stretched my reviewing muscles in preparation for the assault on Mount MOBY (Gabaldon’s acronym for the book, because My Own Heart’s Blood = MOH-B = MOBY, because, Gabaldon) whether I can even treat this book as a book at all. I’ve said it before—these (air quotes) novels are more accurately described as a collection of interwoven stories about connected individuals, with a few thematic elements worked in but with no discernible overarching theme except, perhaps, Love Conquers All But Only If You’re Claire, Jamie Or Their Descendants (Clan Mary Sue). You can’t possibly understand MOBY unless you’ve read (and possibly re-read, as I had to do) the other seven books, as it starts in the middle of a very complicated family situation and gets more involved from there on in. It’s far less of a novel than it is a feeding trough for Outlander fans, and indeed it occurs to me that Gabaldon could probably have more fun simply releasing future episodes of, say, 50 pages at a time as a monthly ebook, à la Dickens. It’s a stable revenue model, and I get the feeling that her writing method is mostly about sitting down and just writing everything that occurs to her within a broadly sketched framework, so it would totally work. Or—OOOO OOOO OOOO—she could do a James Patterson and direct a stable of writers to produce ten Outlander books a year. Where do I apply?<br /><br />OK, so let’s get down to the categories I enumerated above, as this seems to be a fairly good way of organizing my thoughts.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br /><b>Family Secrets.</b> Well, the big one, of course, is William, who spends the entire book suffering from the revelation that he isn’t who he thought he was. And that everyone else seems to have figured that out a long time ago, which is always galling for a young man of William’s age because he’s very clearly at the age when he thinks he knows everything. Things don’t go particularly well for William in this book so he’s generally surly or aggressive throughout, which makes me want to smack him.<br /><br />The side orders of family secrets concern Geilie Duncan and Buck, in a plotline that appears to vanish up its own fundamental orifice just when it’s starting to get interesting, and Fergus, who very sensibly decides not to give a damn about his family secrets and just get on with life, which is what William should do, really.<br /><br /><b>Amazing Escapes.</b> Jamie’s dead! No he’s not. Claire’s dying! No she’s not. Young Ian’s fatally wounded! Or not. Well, we’ve seen it all before, and we know how melodramatic it’s all going to get. And it doesn’t fail to do so. There’s nothing like a mistaken death or near-miss to bring out the maudlin in the surviving character, and it’s a very useful device for getting the reader to shed a little tear and feel like they’ve lived, dammit. It’s notable that when a non-background character DOES die, as a couple of them do, their passing is dealt with rather swiftly and they are then rarely mentioned as their bereaved families get on with the next emergency. I cannot continue this thought without a spoiler I really don’t want to throw in, even within tags, but you’ll see what I mean if you get that far.<br /><br /><b>Sex.</b> I’ll concede that Claire and Jamie have slowed down a little bit, but let’s just say that all that fresh air and exercise, not to mention the near-death experiences, must be very stimulating. And we have two weddings and consequently two wedding nights, not to mention that with the proliferation of points of view comes a proliferation of sexythoughts if not sexytimes, and that minor characters are quite often having sex offstage, as it were, so all in all the eighteenth century continues to be a very lively place. And things get VERY weird when Roger and Buck encounter Geilie (see Time Travel, below). I spotted other, what could be called thematic elements, involving the dual (but not simultaneous) purposes of the male organ, tunnels and dams, and an ode to the penis, but a Freudian analysis of Gabaldon’s oeuvre is both outside the scope of this review and beyond my personal capacities.<br /> <br /><b>Time Travel.</b> As other reviewers have said, the adventures of the MacKenzie family (Bree, Roger, Jem and Mandy) form one of the more entertaining story lines in this book, and go off on a nicely surprising tangent. Alas for the holes in this subplot though—perhaps I wasn’t listening hard enough but I never really saw the point of Rob Cameron’s goons, who appeared to be there merely to increase the dramatic tension. Can someone enlighten me? And then people are developing magical healing powers and telepathy—where is it all leading? And worst of all, given that any trip through the stones is usually accompanied by a hundred pages of leave-taking, apprehension, adventures and the difficulty of acquiring gemstones, HOW did they get from there to there just like that? Have they actually acquired a TARDIS? And are Jem and Mandy a new breed of superhumans? (See Clan Mary Sue, above.)<br /><br /><b>Warfare.</b> We certainly get a comprehensive view of the Revolutionary War, from both sides of the divide, which is interesting and provides plenty of plot fodder. But like a lot of the plotlines in this book, it eventually kind of fizzles. Gabaldon chooses the inconclusive battle of Monmouth as her set piece, after which the characters scatter, presumably to avoid getting caught in another few hundred pages of battle preparation, and the War withdraws to the edges of the plot. I always feel Gabaldon enjoys the lead-up to an event far more than the event itself.<br /><br /><b>Grisly Descriptions of Messy Surgery.</b> I recall a stuck eye, a shredded liver (with interesting insights from the patient’s side of things), the very nasty aftermath of tarring and feathering, an amputation—no, hold on, two amputations—and a double fistula, but there were probably others I’ve forgotten. And dozens of minor ailments, with fascinating asides into unusual uses for mustard and oil of peppermint. This facet of Gabaldon’s work is becoming a bit like the TV series <i>House</i>, which was constantly trying to top its last effort with something even more exotic, except that you could always count on blood and vomit being involved.<br /><br />Well, that just about rounds up the book. Except—the ending. I have a sneaking suspicion that Gabaldon was trying to tie a bow on things just in case she doesn’t get around to writing another Big Enormous Outlander Book, for which I wouldn’t blame her. As I said somewhere above, it might be more worth her while to do e-releases of smaller serial works or offshoots, or, heck, do a JK Rowling and write something different. She’s achieved just about everything a novelist could possibly achieve, after all—once you’ve got a TV series, you’re there.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So where does that leave the reader? Can a series like this ever really end satisfactorily? There are just too many plotlines to tie the whole thing off neatly and with some sort of thematic consistency. And we don’t even seem close to answering the question that should have been answered in book 1—what was the ghost of Jamie doing staring up at Claire’s 1945 window? Dangit, Diana, if you’re going to write one more book, make it THAT one. <br /><br />And yet I’m still giving this gumbo of a novel four stars because the writing’s excellent, the editing’s decent (fewer repeat words and a little tighter overall this time, hooray!) and the stories are generally entertaining. Davina Porter continues to be a stellar audiobook narrator—I absolutely love the way she says “Really?” and “moon”—and her lively voice(s) got me through many hours of running, driving, ironing and chopping vegetables, which are the circumstances under which I generally listen to audiobooks. I wouldn’t hesitate to recommend this series to anyone who has the stamina for it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15682942227776853613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer310434839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1438588309544437786"><br/>Finished June 17, 2014<br/><br/>I was torn about how I felt when I finished this book. I read a few comments on facebook on how others were so happy in some parts and crying in others. ( I didn't read spoilers nor will I put spoilers here either.) I didn't feel any of that. I simply was not pulled into the story emotionally. Which is a shame.<br/><br/>I liked the book generally. The content was there and I adore Gabaldon's writing style - just enough to the imagination. There was enough action to keep me not puttin</span>
  <span id="freeText1438588309544437786" style="display:none"><br />Finished June 17, 2014<br /><br />I was torn about how I felt when I finished this book. I read a few comments on facebook on how others were so happy in some parts and crying in others. ( I didn't read spoilers nor will I put spoilers here either.) I didn't feel any of that. I simply was not pulled into the story emotionally. Which is a shame.<br /><br />I liked the book generally. The content was there and I adore Gabaldon's writing style - just enough to the imagination. There was enough action to keep me not putting the book down.<br /><br />I haven't liked the last couple of books. It has nothing to do with Ms. Gabaldon's story, writing, style, content or anything of that. I think it's more of a personal nature, me enjoying the book. I liked the story and certainly devoured it but I'm starting to suspect that I no longer like the genre or at least the series as much as I used to. I can chalk this up to two major ideas I think. I never connected to Roger, Bree and their family. Any storyline that has them in it bores me. They have a good chunk of story in this book and I read it very fast, if not skipping over a few parts/pages on my Kindle to push through it so I'd get a vague sense of what's going on. <br /><br />I also think I no longer like the genre as I mentioned earlier. I love historical fiction and while this does have some history in it, I feel like the ratio between history and whatever else this could be considered (romance? fiction? family?) is slowly sinking towards a ratio that no longer interests me.<br /><br /><br />Personal opinion, purely no fact based at all...<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This is my personal opinion, but I feel like this book was more of a things that needed to be said to get out of the way before the final book comes out next. There was a lot of stuff going on but it never really went anywhere nor did I feel like there were a lot of conclusions. I'm sure the other reviews mentioned the cliffhanger at the end of the book, just one of these examples. I also started nitpicking on how plausible things that happen really were. It just felt rushed. After following the author on Facebook, I logically know it wasn't rushed, in fact it was delayed several times but that's how I personally felt. I'm disappointed in this book. Maybe I had too high of expectations. Maybe I no longer like the genre or series, or maybe there's just too much of Roger/Bree now to make them enjoyable. I'm glad the series is finishing. I don't think I'd read many more.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />---<br /><br />I can't wait until this book comes out. I've been reading lines that the author posts on Facebook and it's making me want to read it more. I'll start the series again soon so I can get refreshed on the series just in time for the new one to come out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1438588309544437786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_944585317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/944585317" />
    <a title="Tammy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19310939-tammy"><img alt="Tammy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506483769p2/19310939.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/944585317?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tammy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tammy" href="/user/show/19310939-tammy">Tammy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer944585317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer935710710487458496">NOOOOOOOOOOOOOO, I've finished the book! They are not supposed to end! I savored this book, reading it super slow because it deserves it. These books have so much information, so many sub-plots, so many characters, event after event that it is easy to miss some small detail that could be important later if you aren't paying attention. It deserved a slow, deliberate read and that is what I gave it. I would read a few chapters, set the book down, review in my head what I read, think about it some </span>
  <span id="freeText935710710487458496" style="display:none">NOOOOOOOOOOOOOO, I've finished the book! They are not supposed to end! I savored this book, reading it super slow because it deserves it. These books have so much information, so many sub-plots, so many characters, event after event that it is easy to miss some small detail that could be important later if you aren't paying attention. It deserved a slow, deliberate read and that is what I gave it. I would read a few chapters, set the book down, review in my head what I read, think about it some more, go back and read a few more, repeat, then go do something else so I can keep thinking about it. I nearly cried when I was down to the last 100 pages because I honestly did not want it to end.<br /><br />My thoughts about this book.... FREAKING LOVED IT! Duh! As if there was any doubt. Seriously, it was worth the wait. This book gave me a lot of laughs, some tears, some eye rolls, made me want to slap characters, one part confused me at first and then really creeped me out, another part was just gross but all of it was amazing, wonderful, absolutely perfect! I was so immersed in the book that I was feeling what the characters were feeling so if I stopped at a hilarious part I would be in an fun-loving mood but if I stopped at an angry part then I wasn't in such a happy mood and my hubby stayed away from me or, at one point, demanded I read on to get out of that mood. LOL. Yeah I'm that crazy about this series and this book. <br /><br />So, if you haven't pre-ordered the book yet, you definitely need to. If you have, yay! You won't regret it. In the meantime, re-read the EITB to brush up because it has been a while. I did and realized the previous book didn't end where I thought it had and was surprised at what I had forgotten or totally missed the first time around. Brush up and get prepared because in a little over a week you will be reading this book too and loving it just as much!</span>
  <a data-text-id="935710710487458496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/355295683?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Window Seat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Window Seat" href="/user/show/5880804-the-window-seat">The Window Seat</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer355295683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13689477651577066113">After a five year wait, it has finally come. The next chapter in the Outlander series... And with this chapter, I think it is time for me to hang up my "Outlander" hat and bid adieu to these characters.<br/><br/>Jamie and Claire Fraser have been through a lot in the years that they have been together. Falling in love soon after an arranged marriage, Jamie and Claire seem a perfect couple. They love each other very much. But fate - the very thing that brought Claire from the future to the past - stepped in</span>
  <span id="freeText13689477651577066113" style="display:none">After a five year wait, it has finally come. The next chapter in the Outlander series... And with this chapter, I think it is time for me to hang up my "Outlander" hat and bid adieu to these characters.<br /><br />Jamie and Claire Fraser have been through a lot in the years that they have been together. Falling in love soon after an arranged marriage, Jamie and Claire seem a perfect couple. They love each other very much. But fate - the very thing that brought Claire from the future to the past - stepped in and separated them. After decades apart, the two are forging a new life for themselves in the Appalachian Mountains in the New World just as battle is at the gates. This series is a saga of a couple and a family and it is richly detailed with history of the time and the events of the day always play a role in the plot. Surrounding Jamie and Claire are an extensive family - both born and adopted - and as Jamie and Claire continue to live, the souls around them continue to find their own destinies.<br /><br />For the full review, please go to <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.thewindowseat13.com/2014/06/diana-gabaldon-written-in-my-own-hearts.html">http://www.thewindowseat13.com/2014/0...</a></span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fkMyOtJ3rW2T+W3yQ0IyygPwdnuA4SYOZ1UWmz0aMuNEZVvoaSlkBTTS2ZO0tzgV1a+Rs05sqGk8K1Aq8FnAeQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('j+A/CN4apT95fKrtS7x2vKxSkERjlzrISAJqo4WrQa61xlbaZURsV95XHoy8SXxjeg13jK0atK8TfCwSSOizNA==')})
  }
//]]>
